URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS22371200	2018-11-28 14:50:13	25790	species	Golden-crowned Kinglet	Regulus satrapa			2				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Washoe	US-NV-031	US-NV_2211	15			Lower Marlette Creek area (Washoe Co.; Marlette Lake Trail below the switchbacks)	L866938	H	39.1678344	-119.9265701	2004-07-10	04:00:00	obsr16674	S1693546	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	210	4.828		2	1	G189367	0	1	0		John Anderson called me Friday night to discuss plans for a July big day that we had talked about earlier.  We iterated through the state checklist and discussed where the best place to find each bird would be.  I wrote down some species that I had no idea where to find (where does one see Violet-green Swallows in July near Reno?) and planned to do some research and scouting.  "So, when do you want to go?" I asked.  "Is tomorrow OK?", John replied.  So much for planning, but I immediately agreed to have him pick me up at 3:00 AM to head to Lake Tahoe.  On to the birds:----Our general strategy was to pick up mountain birds in the morning, shorebirds and waterbirds in the afternoon, and riparian sage birds in the evening.  We had a difficult time leaving the spectacle of shorebirds at Carson Lake, so our riparian birds were duly neglected. Big misses include Bullock's Oriole, Tree Swallow, House Wren, Townsend's Solitaire, Bushtit,Brewer's Sparrow and Red-breasted Sapsucker.  Not-so-big misses include Blue Grouse, Canyon Wren, Rock Wren, Pinyon Jay, Wood Duck, Black-throated Sparrow, Violet-green Swallow, and Sage Sparrow.  Unexpected surprises included a calling SAW-WHET OWL at Chimney Beach, 20 high-flying WHITE PELICANS over Mt. Rose Meadows, 2 HOODED MERGANSERS at Virginia Lake, and a pair of breeding-plumage COMMON LOONS(!!) on Big Soda Lake in Fallon.
